If the location is absolute, convert it\n   263→        to an RFC 3987 compliant URI and return it. QueryDict(MultiValueDict):\n   543→    \"\"\"\n   544→    A specialized MultiValueDict which represents a query string.\n   545→\n   546→    A QueryDict can be used to represent GET or POST data. It subclasses\n    MultiValueDict since keys in such data can be repeated, for instance\n    in the data from a form with a <select multiple> field.\n\n    By default QueryDicts are immutable, though the copy() method\n    will always return a mutable copy.\n\n    Both keys and values set on this class are converted from the given\n    encoding (DEFAULT_CHARSET by default) to str.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    # These are both reset in __init__, but is specified here at the class\n    # level so that unpickling will have valid values\n    _mutable = True\n    _encoding = None\n\n    def __init__(self, query_string=None, mutable=False, encoding=None):\n        super().__init__()\n        self.encoding = encoding or settings.DEFAULT_CHARSET\n        query_string = query_string or \"\"\n        parse_qsl_kwargs = {\n            \"keep_blank_values\": True,\n            \"encoding\": self.encoding,\n            \"max_num_fields\": settings.DATA_UPLOAD_MAX_NUMBER_FIELDS,\n        }\n        if isinstance(query_string, bytes):\n            # query_string normally contains URL-encoded data, a subset of\n            # ASCII.\n            try:\n                query_string = query_string.decode(self.encoding)\n            except UnicodeDecodeError:\n                # ... but some user agents are misbehaving :-(\n                query_string = query_string.decode(\"iso-8859-1\")\n        try:\n            for key, value in parse_qsl(query_string, **parse_qsl_kwargs):\n                self.appendlist(key, value)\n        except ValueError as e:\n            # ValueError can also be raised if the strict_parsing argument to\n            # parse_qsl() is True. QueryDict(MultiValueDict):\n   543→    \"\"\"\n   544→    A specialized MultiValueDict which represents a query string.\n   545→\n   546→    A QueryDict can be used to represent GET or POST data. It subclasses\n   547→    MultiValueDict since keys in such data can be repeated, for instance\n   548→    in the data from a form with a <select multiple> field.\n   549→\n   550→    By default QueryDicts are immutable, though the copy() method\n   551→    will always return a mutable copy.\n   552→\n   553→    Both keys and values set on this class are converted from the given\n   554→    encoding (DEFAULT_CHARSET by default) to str.\n   555→    \"\"\"\n   556→\n   557→    # These are both reset in __init__, but is specified here at the class\n   558→    # level so that unpickling will have valid values\n   559→    _mutable = True\n   560→    _encoding = None\n   561→\n   562→    def __init__(self, query_string=None, mutable=False, encoding=None):\n   563→        super().__init__()\n   564→        self.encoding = encoding or settings.DEFAULT_CHARSET\n   565→        query_string = query_string or \"\"\n   566→        parse_qsl_kwargs = {\n   567→            \"keep_blank_values\": True,\n   568→            \"encoding\": self.encoding,\n   569→            \"max_num_fields\": settings.DATA_UPLOAD_MAX_NUMBER_FIELDS,\n   570→        }\n   571→        if isinstance(query_string, bytes):\n   572→            # query_string normally contains URL-encoded data, a subset of\n   573→            # ASCII.\n   574→            try:\n   575→                query_string = query_string.decode(self.encoding)\n   576→            except UnicodeDecodeError:\n   577→                # ... but some user agents are misbehaving :-(\n   578→                query_string = query_string.decode(\"iso-8859-1\")\n   579→        try:\n   580→            for key, value in parse_qsl(query_string, **parse_qsl_kwargs):\n   581→                self.appendlist(key, value)\n   582→        except ValueError as e:\n   583→            # ValueError can also be raised if the strict_parsing argument to\n   584→            # parse_qsl() is True.
